<p><i><b>Relapse</b></i> is the sixth <a href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album" class="mw-redirect">studio album</a> by American rapper <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, released on May 15, 2009 by <a href="/wiki/Shady_Records" title="Shady Records">Shady Records</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>. It was his first album of original material since <i><a href="/wiki/Encore_(Eminem_album)" title="Encore (Eminem album)">Encore</a></i> (2004), following a four-year hiatus from recording due to his <a href="/wiki/Writer%27s_block" title="Writer's block">writer's block</a> and an addiction to prescription sleeping medication. Recording sessions for the album took place during 2007 to 2009 at several recording studios, and <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Batson" title="Mark Batson">Mark Batson</a>, and Eminem handled production. Conceptually, <i>Relapse</i> concerns the ending of his <a href="/wiki/Drug_rehabilitation" title="Drug rehabilitation">drug rehabilitation</a>, rapping after a non-fictional <a href="/wiki/Relapse" title="Relapse">relapse</a>, and the return of his Slim Shady alter-ego.</p>
<p>One of the most anticipated album releases of 2009, <i>Relapse</i> debuted at number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, selling 608,000 copies in its first week. It produced three singles that attained chart success and has been certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">double platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a>. The album received mixed reviews from most music critics, who were divided in their responses towards Eminem's lyrics. It has sold more than two million copies in the United States and more than five million copies worldwide.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Relapse_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since 2005, Eminem intended to take a break from recording his own music to become a <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_production" title="Hip hop production">hip hop producer</a> for other rap acts, especially for the artists signed on his own label Shady Records.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> However, Eminem entered his hiatus after cancelling the European leg of the <a href="/wiki/Anger_Management_Tour" title="Anger Management Tour">Anger Management Tour</a> in the summer of 2005 because of exhaustion and an addiction to prescription sleeping drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> In the following year, the rapper's remarriage to his former wife Kimberly Scott lasted only eleven weeks before a second divorce,<sup id="cite_ref-observer_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-observer-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> while his closest friend and fellow rapper <a href="/wiki/Proof_(rapper)" title="Proof (rapper)">DeShaun "Proof" Holton</a> was later shot and killed during an altercation outside a <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a> nightclub. Devastated, Eminem relapsed into <a href="/wiki/Prescription_drug" title="Prescription drug">prescription drug</a> <a href="/wiki/Drug_abuse" title="Drug abuse" class="mw-redirect">abuse</a> and became increasingly reclusive.<sup id="cite_ref-observer_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-observer-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indep_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indep-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-covertmtv_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-covertmtv-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> In a June 2009 interview for <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a></i>, Eminem elaborated on the impact of Proof's death on him, stating:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"Everyone felt [Proof's] loss, from his kids, to his wife, to everyone. But, for some reason, in hindsight, the way I felt was almost like it happened to just me... Maybe at the time I was a little bit selfish with it. I think it kind of hit me so hard. It just blindsided me. I just went into such a dark place that, with everything, the drugs, my thoughts, everything. And the more drugs I consumed, and it was all depressants I was taking, the more depressed I became, the more self-loathing I became..."<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Speculation on an upcoming album by Eminem was reported since mid–2007 from announcements made by artists <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stat_Quo" title="Stat Quo">Stat Quo</a>, former members of Shady Records.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Also, rapper <a href="/wiki/Bizarre_(rapper)" title="Bizarre (rapper)">Bizarre</a>&#160;– a member of the hip hop group <a href="/wiki/D12" title="D12">D12</a>&#160;– stated that the release of the group's third studio album was on hold because <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a> wanted to release Eminem's album first.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> By the end of the year, additional musicians associated with Shady Records&#160;– including <a href="/wiki/The_Alchemist_(producer)" title="The Alchemist (producer)" class="mw-redirect">The Alchemist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bishop_Lamont" title="Bishop Lamont">Bishop Lamont</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cashis" title="Cashis">Cashis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Obie_Trice" title="Obie Trice">Obie Trice</a>&#160;– had confirmed on different occasions that the rapper was effectively working on a new album.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cashisvid_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cashisvid-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> On September 12, 2007, during a call at the radio station <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">WQHT</a> <i>Hot 97</i>, Eminem stated that he was in limbo and was not sure whether he would release any new material in the near future. He then elaborated that at that point he was constantly working in the recording studio and had come to terms with his personal issues.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> However, in December 2007, he was hospitalized because of an <a href="/wiki/Drug_overdose" title="Drug overdose">overdose</a> of <a href="/wiki/Methadone" title="Methadone">methadone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> In early 2008, he began a <a href="/wiki/12-step_program" title="12-step program" class="mw-redirect">12-step program</a> to recover from his addiction; in a later interview, he said he has been sober since April 20, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording">Recording</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Relapse_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recording">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the initial recording stages of <i>Relapse</i>, <a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">record producer</a> and long-time Detroit collaborator Jeff Bass of the <a href="/wiki/Bass_Brothers" title="Bass Brothers">Bass Brothers</a> worked with Eminem on 25 tracks, two years after the rapper had received treatment for his sleeping pill addiction in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-indep_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indep-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McCollum_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCollum-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Depressed by Proof's death, Eminem fell into a period of "<a href="/wiki/Writer%27s_block" title="Writer's block">writer's block</a>", where he felt everything he wrote was not worth recording.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> To compensate for this, Bass chose to follow a production style that would allow the artist to rap "off the top of his head, as opposed to writing a story".<sup id="cite_ref-McCollum_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCollum-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Eminem would then <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_rap" title="Freestyle rap">freestyle</a> or record vocals one line at a time before interrupting and then recording another line.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> At the same time, according to Eminem's song rights supervisor Joel Martin, the rapper began to collect additional songs without noticing it. He would often record or produce material initially intended for the musical projects of other artists, but end up with tracks he really liked.<sup id="cite_ref-McCollum_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCollum-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_(Eminem_song)" title="Beautiful (Eminem song)">Beautiful</a>", produced by Eminem, was the only song on <i>Relapse</i> that was recorded in these years while he was not sober.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Eminem purchased the Effigy Studio in <a href="/wiki/Ferndale,_Michigan" title="Ferndale, Michigan">Ferndale, Michigan</a>, in 2007, and ended his working relationship with much of his former production team of the 54 Sound <a href="/wiki/Recording_studio" title="Recording studio">recording studio</a>, including the Bass Brothers.<sup id="cite_ref-McCollum_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCollum-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2007, Dr. Dre stated his intention to dedicate two months to the production of <i>Relapse</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-nme_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nme-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Working with Dr. Dre allowed Eminem to concentrate on the processes of songwriting rather than the production, which was largely taken care of by Dre.<sup id="cite_ref-nme_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nme-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The rapper justified his choice of using Dr. Dre for the vast majority of the production due to their long collaborative history and a musical "chemistry" only he and Dr. Dre shared.<sup id="cite_ref-DecBillboard_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DecBillboard-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> This allowed the rapper to pick the <a href="/wiki/Beat_(music)" title="Beat (music)">beats</a> from Dr. Dre's catalog that challenged him <a href="/wiki/Rhythm" title="Rhythm">rhythm</a>-wise to experiment with different <a href="/wiki/Flow_(music)" title="Flow (music)" class="mw-redirect">flows</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rs3am_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rs3am-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The making of the album progressed at the Effigy Studio up to a year after, as recording sessions were then moved to <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando, Florida</a> in September 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-indep_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indep-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-xxl_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> By then, Eminem had begun to start writing verses again at such a pace that he often took more time to record the lyrics than write them. He credited <a href="/wiki/Sobriety" title="Sobriety">sobriety</a> for his new creative run, acknowledging that his mind was free of the clutter that "blocked" him during his drug abuse in the last years.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Dr. Dre would start the song-writing process by giving a number of his beats on a CD to Eminem, who in a separate room in the studio would listen and select the ones he preferred and inspired him the most. Eminem would then write lyrics to the instrumentals, while Dr. Dre and his production staff continued to create new music. Once he felt he had written lyrics for enough songs, Eminem would dedicate an entire day to record his songs to the point that he would lose his voice for the following days. At that point, the rapper would then begin to write lyrics for new songs.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prelapse_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelapse-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> The process continued for the next six months and allowed Eminem to have enough material also for a second album <i><a href="/wiki/Relapse_2" title="Relapse 2" class="mw-redirect">Relapse&#160;2</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-UMG_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UMG-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During this recording period, a handful of songs intended for <i>Relapse</i> were <a href="/wiki/Internet_leak" title="Internet leak">leaked</a> on the Internet, including an incomplete version of "<a href="/wiki/Crack_a_Bottle" title="Crack a Bottle">Crack a Bottle</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-DecBillboard_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DecBillboard-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> The song was finished in January 2009 and featured vocals from Dr. Dre and 50 Cent.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite the leak, the album was being completed in a state of near-total secrecy, according to the British newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-indep_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indep-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Even <a href="/wiki/Polydor_Records" title="Polydor Records">Polydor Records</a>, the multinational owner of Interscope, had no information on the album at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-indep_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indep-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> On April 23, Eminem suggested he and possibly Dr. Dre were the only ones in possession of the final copy of <i>Relapse</i>; his manager <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rosenberg_(music_manager)" title="Paul Rosenberg (music manager)">Paul Rosenberg</a> added that even Eminem's record labels were not in possession of the music less than a month before its release to prevent possible <a href="/wiki/Bootleg_recording" title="Bootleg recording">bootlegging</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3amshade45_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3amshade45-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Relapse_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="mbox-small" style="border:1px solid #aaa; background-color:#f9f9f9;">

<td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em;"><span style="font-size:smaller;"><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>

</table>
<p>In an interview for <a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)"><i>XXL</i></a>, Eminem described the concept behind <i>Relapse</i> to be the ending of his <a href="/wiki/Drug_rehabilitation" title="Drug rehabilitation">drug rehabilitation</a> and thus rap as if he was on drugs again, as well as the return of his fictional <a href="/wiki/Alter-ego" title="Alter-ego" class="mw-redirect">alter-ego</a> Slim Shady.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the interviewer Datwon Thomas, Eminem's influences for the album came from his own past drug issues and from television shows and documentaries involving crime and <a href="/wiki/Serial_killer" title="Serial killer">serial killers</a>, as the rapper was fascinated by "serial killers and their <a href="/wiki/Psyche_(psychology)" title="Psyche (psychology)">psyche</a> and their mind states".<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> In a May 2009 interview for <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, Eminem discussed his view of serial killers, stating:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"You listen to these people talk, or you see them, they look so regular. What does a serial killer look like? He don’t look like anything. He looks like you. You could be living next door to one. If I lived next door to you, you could be."<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Music critic <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> interpreted the opening line to the album featuring the phrase "horror corridor" as Eminem telling listeners that it is a <a href="/wiki/Horrorcore" title="Horrorcore">horrorcore</a> album.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Ben Kaplan of the <i><a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Courier" title="Vancouver Courier">Vancouver Courier</a></i> also categorized it as a horrorcore album.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ann_Powers" title="Ann Powers">Ann Powers</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> said that the album's "horrorcore scenes" show Eminem as "a madman created by the hypocrisy of therapy."<sup id="cite_ref-latimesreview_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimesreview-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Content">Content</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Relapse_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Content">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Relapse</i> opens with the skit "Dr. West", where actor <a href="/wiki/Dominic_West" title="Dominic West">Dominic West</a> voices a drug counselor whose untrustworthiness causes Eminem to fall back to drugs and the return to his Slim Shady character.<sup id="cite_ref-latimesreview_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimesreview-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thesunreview_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thesunreview-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> The skit leads to "<a href="/wiki/3_a.m._(Eminem_song)" title="3 a.m. (Eminem song)">3 a.m.</a>", where Eminem depicts himself as a <a href="/wiki/Serial_killer" title="Serial killer">serial killer</a> during a murder spree.<sup id="cite_ref-nme2_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nme2-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> When "3 a.m." was released as a single prior to the album's own release, Eminem noted that the song closely mirrored what he believed was the overall dark tone of the album.<sup id="cite_ref-rs3am_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rs3am-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> On "My Mom", the rapper traces his addictive tendencies to his mother and shows how he became a drug addict just like her.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_16-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rsreview_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsreview-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Eminem continues his family tales on "Insane", where he imagines himself as a victim of <a href="/wiki/Child_molestation" title="Child molestation" class="mw-redirect">child molestation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thesunreview_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thesunreview-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> For Eminem, the goal of "Insane" was to make song that would disgust the listeners and "make them puke", adding that he came up with this idea after thinking of the song's first line ("I was born with a dick in my brain/Yeah, fucked in the head").<sup id="cite_ref-prelapse_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelapse-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a> and her current husband <a href="/wiki/Nick_Cannon" title="Nick Cannon">Nick Cannon</a> are targeted in "Bagpipes from Baghdad", where Eminem raps over a <a href="/wiki/Pungi" title="Pungi">pungi</a> <a href="/wiki/Music_loop" title="Music loop" class="mw-redirect">loop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-amreview_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amreview-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ewreview_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ewreview-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After "Hello", where Eminem re-introduces himself after years of being absent "mentally",<sup id="cite_ref-prelapse_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelapse-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> he continues his violent fantasies on "Same Song &amp; Dance", where he abducts and murders <a href="/wiki/Lindsay_Lohan" title="Lindsay Lohan">Lindsay Lohan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rsreview_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsreview-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-amreview_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amreview-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Upbeat" title="Upbeat" class="mw-redirect">upbeat</a> rhythm of "Same Song &amp; Dance" reminded Eminem of a dance track, which inspired him to write something in order to "get women to dance to it and not really know what the fuck they're dancing to" without listening to the lyrics.<sup id="cite_ref-prelapse_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelapse-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> On the ninth track of the album, "<a href="/wiki/We_Made_You" title="We Made You">We Made You</a>", Eminem mocks several celebrities and plays the role of a "pop star serial killer".<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Eminem noted that his various "celebrity bashings" were not meant to be seen as personal attacks, but it was rather "picking names out of a hat" that rhymed with the words he wanted to use during the writing process.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> On "Medicine Ball" Eminem mocks and impersonates deceased actor <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Reeve" title="Christopher Reeve">Christopher Reeve</a> in order to get his audience to "laugh at it, and then almost feel bad for laughing".<sup id="cite_ref-prelapse_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelapse-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rsreview_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsreview-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The next track is "Stay Wide Awake", which Eminem raps about <a href="/wiki/Sexual_assault" title="Sexual assault">assaulting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">raping</a> women. Dr. Dre also has a <a href="/wiki/Guest_appearance" title="Guest appearance">guest appearance</a> on "<a href="/wiki/Old_Time%27s_Sake" title="Old Time's Sake">Old Time's Sake</a>", a duet Eminem described as a "fun, yet reminiscent record old times" in which he and Dre rap back and forth between each other, advocating the use of marijuana for creative and financial benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-prelapse_24-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelapse-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Song "Must Be the Ganja" follows, where Eminem raps that working in the recording studio is like a drug and an addiction for him.<sup id="cite_ref-prelapse_24-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelapse-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After the skit "Mr. Mathers", where Eminem is recovered to a hospital, "Déjà Vu" addresses his overdose in 2007 and drug dependency during his hiatus from music.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_16-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prelapse_24-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelapse-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> On the song, Eminem also explains how this has affected him in the last five years, to the point where his daughter has become scared of her father's behavior.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> "Beautiful", a <a href="/wiki/Ballad" title="Ballad">ballad</a> which samples "Reaching Out" by <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers">Rock Therapy</a>, also deals with the same time period where Eminem believed he had "reached rock bottom" and lost hope for his future.<sup id="cite_ref-prelapse_24-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelapse-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rsreview_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsreview-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Eminem felt it was important to include "Beautiful" on the album as a reminder to himself as well as "anybody who is in a dark place [...] that you can get out of it".<sup id="cite_ref-prelapse_24-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelapse-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> After "Crack a Bottle", a collaboration with Dr. Dre and 50 Cent, <i>Relapse</i> ends with "Underground". On this final track, Eminem sought to bring back to his music and lyrics the subject matter and punchlines reminiscent of "The Hiphop Shop times" (The Hiphop Shop was a clothing store in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a> where local rappers, including Eminem, would compete in <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_battles" title="Freestyle battles" class="mw-redirect">freestyle battles</a><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>), before he had become famous and thus did not have worry about the explicit content of his lyrics.<sup id="cite_ref-prelapse_24-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelapse-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relapse:_Refill_and_Relapse_2"><i>Relapse: Refill</i> and <i>Relapse 2</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Relapse_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Relapse: Refill and Relapse 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="infobox vevent haudio" cellspacing="3" style="border-spacing:3px;width:22em;">

<p>Because Eminem recorded far more material than he could use for one album and felt that he had to offer his fans more music after staying on hiatus for so long, fellow D12 member Swift confirmed that Eminem in fact had planned to put out two albums the same year, following with <i>Relapse&#160;2</i>, in late 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-dashadyspot.com_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dashadyspot.com-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Angela Yee's <a href="/wiki/Shade_45" title="Shade 45">Shade 45</a> interview with Eminem on April&#160;23, 2009, <i>Relapse&#160;2</i> was to be a continuation of <i>Relapse</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> During the interview, Eminem confirmed: "It's extremely close to being finished, it just depends on how many songs I want to put on it."<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Eminem also explained the album was more "emotionally driven" than <i>Relapse</i>, which was, as he explains, "[just] rap records".<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Guest appearances were expected to come from the likes of <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>, <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>, <a href="/wiki/D12" title="D12">D12</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royce_da_5%279%22" title="Royce da 5'9&quot;">Royce da 5'9"</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Banks" title="Lloyd Banks">Lloyd Banks</a><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Cashis" title="Cashis">Cashis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was subsequently pushed back for an early 2010 release, so Eminem decided to re-release <i>Relapse</i> as <i>Relapse: Refill</i> with seven new tracks, including the single "<a href="/wiki/Forever_(Drake_song)" title="Forever (Drake song)">Forever</a>" (originally on <a href="/wiki/Music_Inspired_by_More_Than_a_Game" title="Music Inspired by More Than a Game" class="mw-redirect"><i>More Than a Game</i> soundtrack</a>) and "Taking My Ball" (released with <i><a href="/wiki/DJ_Hero" title="DJ Hero">DJ Hero</a></i>), as well as five previously unreleased tracks. On its re-release, Eminem stated: "I want to deliver more material for the fans this year like I originally planned. Hopefully these tracks on <i>The Refill</i> will tide the fans over until we put out <i>Relapse&#160;2</i> next year."<sup id="cite_ref-rapradar.com_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rapradar.com-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On April 13, 2010, Eminem tweeted "There is no <i>Relapse&#160;2</i>", thus announcing that the album has been scrapped in favor of his new project <i><a href="/wiki/Recovery_(Eminem_album)" title="Recovery (Eminem album)">Recovery</a></i>. While recording <i>Relapse&#160;2</i> and witnessing the mixed reaction of its predecessor among fans and critics alike, Eminem decided to throw away most of the recorded material and started from scratch. The result did not seem to him as continuation of <i>Relapse</i> but more of an individual project that deserved its own name. Eminem said: "I had originally planned for <i>Relapse&#160;2</i> to come out last year. But as I kept recording and working with new producers, the idea of a sequel to <i>Relapse</i> started to make less and less sense to me, and I wanted to make a completely new album. The music on <i>Recovery</i> came out very different from <i>Relapse</i>, and I think it deserves its own title."<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The now-renamed album debuted at number 1 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i>&#160;200</a> chart, with first-week sales of 741,000&#160;copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> As of September&#160;25, 2011, the album had sold 4,040,000&#160;copies in the United States<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> and was also the best-selling album of 2010 worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> earning a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Best_Rap_Album" title="Best Rap Album" class="mw-redirect">Best Rap Album</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_and_promotion">Release and promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Relapse_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Release and promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Popsomp_Hills_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Popsomp_Hills_1.JPG/198px-Popsomp_Hills_1.JPG" width="198" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Popsomp_Hills_1.JPG/297px-Popsomp_Hills_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Popsomp_Hills_1.JPG/396px-Popsomp_Hills_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Popsomp_Hills_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
"Popsomp Hills", a fictional <a href="/wiki/Drug_rehabilitation" title="Drug rehabilitation">rehabilitation center</a> established to promote <i>Relapse</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2007, Shady Records rapper Cashis discussed the album, referring to it by the title <i>King Mathers</i> and adding that it would be released later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-cashisvid_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cashisvid-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> However, Eminem's publicist Dennis Dennehy would later deny this and stated that "there [was] no album scheduled for a 2007 release" and that, as of August&#160;2007, there was no confirmed title.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> No other official statement was made for over a year. It was not until September 15, 2008, at an event held by <a href="/wiki/Shade_45" title="Shade 45">Shade 45</a> to celebrate the publication of Eminem's autobiography <i><a href="/wiki/The_Way_I_Am_(autobiography)" title="The Way I Am (autobiography)" class="mw-redirect">The Way I Am</a></i>, the rapper confirmed his plans to release a studio album by the title of <i>Relapse</i>. During the party, he also previewed to the audience a song called "I'm Having a Relapse".<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In regards to the album's release date, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> wrote in its October&#160;2008 issue that <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Megastores" title="Virgin Megastores">Virgin Megastores</a> had planned to distribute <i>Relapse</i> on November&#160;27, 2008 in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 27, a spokesperson for Interscope explained that there was no official date at the time, and that any release dates that had been posted on any website were unfounded.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> In a phone conversation during the finale of <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">Total Request Live</a></i> on November 16, 2008, Eminem asserted that <i>Relapse</i> would be released during the <a href="/wiki/Calendar_year" title="Calendar year">first quarter</a> of 2009, precisely during either of the first two months of the year, explaining that he was in the process of selecting the songs for the album.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the leak two months before, "<a href="/wiki/Crack_a_Bottle" title="Crack a Bottle">Crack a Bottle</a>" was eventually released for legal paid <a href="/wiki/Music_download" title="Music download">digital download</a> as well as a <a href="/wiki/Promotional_recording" title="Promotional recording">promotional single</a> on February 2, 2009, and also reached the number one position on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> according to Eminem's manager Paul Rosenberg, a music video for the song had been produced and directed by Syndrome and was released in several parts of the world from May to early June. At the time of the release, various contradicting reports disputed whether the song would be included on <i>Relapse</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-crackvid_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crackvid-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> but a press release from head label <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a> confirmed the single's inclusion on the album.<sup id="cite_ref-UMG_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UMG-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> In similar press statements after March 5, Universal made public the regional release dates for <i>Relapse</i>: as early as May 15, 2009, in Italy and the Netherlands; most other European countries and Brazil on May 18; and the following day in the United States and Australia. Additionally, the record label also announced a second album by Eminem, then called <i>Relapse 2</i> but later titled <i><a href="/wiki/Recovery_(Eminem_album)" title="Recovery (Eminem album)">Recovery</a></i>, which was to be released by the end of the year, but expected in June 2010. Eminem explained that he and Dr. Dre had recorded a considerable amount of music and thus, by releasing two albums, would allow listeners to have access to all of his music.<sup id="cite_ref-UMG_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UMG-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After the release of "Crack a Bottle", the music video of the single "<a href="/wiki/We_Made_You" title="We Made You">We Made You</a>" was aired on April&#160;7, and became available for purchase a week later on April&#160;13.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The video was directed by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kahn" title="Joseph Kahn">Joseph Kahn</a> and premiered simultaneously on several <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> channels as well as MTV's website.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> On April&#160;28, the third overall single for the album, "3&#160;a.m.", was released again for paid music download.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> A music video for "3&#160;a.m." was directed by Syndrome and filmed in Detroit. It premiered on May 2 on <a href="/wiki/Cinemax" title="Cinemax">Cinemax</a>, several days after a <a href="/wiki/Teaser_trailer" title="Teaser trailer" class="mw-redirect">trailer</a> for the video was posted online.<sup id="cite_ref-rs3am_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rs3am-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Two more singles were distributed prior to the album's release, as "<a href="/wiki/Old_Time%27s_Sake" title="Old Time's Sake">Old Time's Sake</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_(Eminem_song)" title="Beautiful (Eminem song)">Beautiful</a>" went on sale on the <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a> on May&#160;5 and May&#160;12 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-RRtrack_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RRtrack-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> "My Darling" and "Careful What You Wish For" were made available upon purchase of the Premium version of the album.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The track "Insane" peaked at position 85 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart on the album's release via iTunes.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On April&#160;4, 2009, <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> featured Eminem during the network's coverage of the <a href="/wiki/2009_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="2009 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">2009 NCAA Final Four</a> in a segment where he recited the <a href="/wiki/Spoken_word" title="Spoken word">spoken word</a> "Love Letter to Detroit". Later on the same day, the rapper inducted the hip hop group <a href="/wiki/Run-D.M.C." title="Run-D.M.C." class="mw-redirect">Run-D.M.C.</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>. Adam Graham of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Detroit_News" title="The Detroit News">The Detroit News</a></i> described this as "all part of the calculated promotional push" for <i>Relapse</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> The rapper performed live at the <a href="/wiki/2009_MTV_Movie_Awards" title="2009 MTV Movie Awards">2009 MTV Movie Awards</a> on May&#160;31,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> while he appeared on the covers of hip hop magazines <a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)"><i>Vibe</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)"><i>XXL</i></a> in their respective issues in June&#160;2009;<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_7-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> the latter was created by a deal struck with Eminem and <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel Comics</a>, where the rapper would pose as Marvel's main vigilante <a href="/wiki/Punisher_(comics)" title="Punisher (comics)" class="mw-redirect">The Punisher</a>. Marvel created an issue of the comic co-starring Eminem.<sup id="cite_ref-punisher_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punisher-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a> game to accompany the album was released on May&#160;19, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>While on the Never Say Never tour, fellow group members Swifty and Kuniva (D12) along with Royce Da 5'9" stopped by KISS 100FM for a live interview and spoke on <i>Relapse</i>. Royce stated that the album will be a game changer and jokingly said he might have to push his own album back three years after Eminem drops his.<sup id="cite_ref-dashadyspot.com_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dashadyspot.com-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Kuniva added that D12 recorded many tracks for <i>Relapse</i> but wasn't sure if they would make the album or not.<sup id="cite_ref-dashadyspot.com_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dashadyspot.com-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Swifty then confirmed that Eminem would be dropping two albums in 2009, with <i>Relapse 2</i> following <i>Relapse</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-dashadyspot.com_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dashadyspot.com-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Relapse</i> was re-released on December&#160;21, 2009, as <i>Relapse: Refill</i>, with seven bonus tracks and including the single "<a href="/wiki/Forever_(Drake_song)" title="Forever (Drake song)">Forever</a>" (originally on <a href="/wiki/Music_Inspired_by_More_Than_a_Game" title="Music Inspired by More Than a Game" class="mw-redirect"><i>More Than a Game</i> soundtrack</a>), "Taking My Ball" (released with <i><a href="/wiki/DJ_Hero" title="DJ Hero">DJ Hero</a></i>), and five previously unreleased tracks. On its re-release, Eminem stated: "I want to deliver more material for the fans this year like I originally planned. Hopefully these tracks on <i>The Refill</i> will tide the fans over until we put out <i>Relapse 2</i> next year".<sup id="cite_ref-rapradar.com_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rapradar.com-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Artwork">Artwork</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Relapse_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Artwork">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Album_cover" title="Album cover">album cover</a> for <i>Relapse</i> was first published through Eminem's <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> account on April&#160;21, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-covertmtv_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-covertmtv-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> It illustrates a head shot of the rapper composed by a mosaic of thousands of pills. A sticker on the cover resembles a prescription drug label, on which the patient is Eminem and the prescribing doctor is Dr. Dre.<sup id="cite_ref-covertmtv_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-covertmtv-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Gil Kaufman of <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a> described the cover as a reference to the rapper's struggle and addiction to prescription drugs, adding that it follows Eminem's habit of displaying personal issues in his art.<sup id="cite_ref-covertmtv_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-covertmtv-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> The album booklet and back cover follow a pill prescription design. On the backside of the booklet is a dedication to Proof, where Eminem explains that he's sober and that he tried to write a song for him, but that he didn't find one of them good enough therefore he dedicates the whole album to him. The CD itself is meant to represent the lid on a bottle of prescription pills, grey with the big red inscription "Push Down &amp; Turn".<sup id="cite_ref-booklet_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-booklet-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The cover for <i>Relapse: Refill</i> is the same, with the background color changed from black to white. The prescription drug label is scratched out and the writing "Refill" is posed next to it.<sup id="cite_ref-booklet_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-booklet-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Relapse_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>One of the most anticipated albums of 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Relapse</i> was the top-selling hip hop album of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon its release, the album debuted at number 1 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, selling 608,000 copies in its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> In Canada, the album sold 64,000 copies in its first week and debuted at number 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> Outside of North America, <i>Relapse</i> managed to reach the number one spot in its first week in various other countries including Australia, France, Norway, Denmark and New Zealand,<sup id="cite_ref-Eminem:_Relapse_.28Chart-positions.29_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eminem:_Relapse_.28Chart-positions.29-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> while climbing into the Top 5 in many other countries, including Germany, Italy, Finland, Spain, Belgium, the Netherlands, Austria, Switzerland and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-Eminem:_Relapse_.28Chart-positions.29_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eminem:_Relapse_.28Chart-positions.29-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eminem:_Relapse_.28Chart-position_for_Germany.29_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eminem:_Relapse_.28Chart-position_for_Germany.29-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> In its second week the album stayed at number one and sold a further 211,000&#160;copies, taking its total to 819,000 to become the fifth best-seller of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> In the third week, <i>Relapse</i> dropped to number two and sold another 141,000 copies, bringing the total U.S. sales to 962,000,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Relapse</i> dropped to number three in its fourth week, selling 87,000&#160;copies for a total of 1,049,000 in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The next week, <i>Relapse</i> went down to number four and sold 72,000&#160;copies.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> In its sixth week, the album was at number five and sold another 47,000&#160;copies, pushing its total sales to 1,169,000.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> It dropped down to the number nine in its seventh week, selling 39,000&#160;copies and taking its total U.S. sales up to 1,207,000&#160;copies.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> In its eighth week, it remained at number nine and sold a further 34,000&#160;copies for a total of 1,241,000.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Relapse</i> became the best selling rap album of 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Relapse</i> had sold more than two million copies in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-XXL-DP_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XXL-DP-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jacobs_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jacobs-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">double platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> on August 27, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> By June 2010, it had sold more than 5&#160;million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Relapse</i> has sold more than 2,363,000 units to date in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Relapse_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a></td>
<td style="vertical-align:middle"><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="2.5/5 stars"><img alt="2.5/5 stars" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110" /><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" width="11" height="11" <tr>
<td scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i></td>
<td style="vertical-align:middle">4/10<sup id="cite_ref-Spin_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spin-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>Relapse</i> received generally mixed reviews from music critics.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Metacritic_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metacritic-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> It holds an aggregate score of 59, based on 27 reviews, at <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Metacritic_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metacritic-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite calling it an "impressively focused and clever work", <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> writer <a href="/wiki/Ann_Powers" title="Ann Powers">Ann Powers</a> felt the music was "not transcendent" and commented that "Eminem could have pulled his music into a new category. What he presents is still powerful, but narrowly cast".<sup id="cite_ref-Powers_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Powers-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> Andy Gill of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> found the album to be "drably repetitive, while its dated tone is emphasised by the return of Dr Dre as producer."<sup id="cite_ref-Gill_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gill-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i><span style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Louis Pattison found Eminem's wordplay "wicked in the depths of its depravity", but felt that "the overriding feel is of an album just too jaded, too joyless to truly count as a return to form".<sup id="cite_ref-Pattison_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pattison-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a>'s Eric Henderson viewed that "the further <i>Relapse</i> strays from narrative veracity, the more one suspects his fanbase feels he's tapping into his bottomless well for horror-show grandstanding."<sup id="cite_ref-smreview_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smreview-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> called <i>Relapse</i> "an album that sits square between what Eminem is theoretically still capable of and what we feared he has become."<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Rabin" title="Nathan Rabin">Nathan Rabin</a>, writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a></i>, panned it as "facile pre-adolescent shock mixed with gory, corpse-strewn, <i><a href="/wiki/Fangoria_(magazine)" title="Fangoria (magazine)" class="mw-redirect">Fangoria</a></i>-damaged horrorcore."<sup id="cite_ref-avclub_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-avclub-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MSN_Music" title="MSN Music">MSN Music</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> called it a "dud" and accused Eminem of <a href="/wiki/Sensationalism" title="Sensationalism">sensationalism</a>: "this is not a Slim Shady album. Slim Shady had a lightness about him".<sup id="cite_ref-Christgau_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christgau-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a positive review, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> writer <a href="/wiki/Rob_Sheffield" title="Rob Sheffield">Rob Sheffield</a> called the album a "more painful, honest and vital record", viewing it as on-par with Eminem's acclaimed fourth album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Eminem_Show" title="The Eminem Show">The Eminem Show</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-rsreview_35-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsreview-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> of <a href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic" class="mw-redirect">Allmusic</a> described the album as "musically white-hot, dense, and dramatic" and said that "his flow is so good, his wordplay so sharp, it seems churlish to wish that he addressed something other than his long-standing obsessions and demons".<sup id="cite_ref-amreview_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amreview-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> commended its honest depiction of Eminem's drug addiction and overuse.<sup id="cite_ref-tdtreview_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdtreview-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> Although he found its concept "spotty", <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i><span style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Benjamin Meadows-Ingram praised Eminem's lyricism, writing that "Em works wonders with words, expanding the boundaries of the art of rap itself [...] the composition is experimental and abstract, a master toying with form".<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/52nd_Grammy_Awards" title="52nd Grammy Awards" class="mw-redirect">52nd Grammy Awards</a>, the album won a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retrospect">Retrospect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Relapse_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Retrospect">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On his following album <i><a href="/wiki/Recovery_(Eminem_album)" title="Recovery (Eminem album)">Recovery</a></i> (2010), Eminem made reference to <i>Relapse</i> and criticizes it in the second verse of the song "<a href="/wiki/Not_Afraid" title="Not Afraid">Not Afraid</a>": "In fact, let's be honest/That last <i>Relapse</i> CD was 'ehh'/ Perhaps I ran them accents into the ground/ Relax, I ain't going back to that now".<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>He slowed down his feelings about the album after that saying "I don’t hate <i>Relapse</i>. I don’t hate it at all, but when I’m looking back at an album I do have a tendency, and especially with that album, to run things into the ground. That was one of those instances where I got in a zone, like, “Yo I just want to be this demented serial killer on this album.” And part of that was a growing process to get to <i>Recovery</i>, working through those steps, relearning how to rap, and relearning where I need to be at."<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> He reiterates this statement during his 2013 Q&amp;A with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> saying "I don't hate the record. I want to rap and be able to always try to do my best lyrically, but at the same time find the right balance between that and making the right songs. And you know, I don't know if I necessarily found that balance yet, because I was just getting sober and just kind of finding my feet again and so there was a lot of songs that were just like "Ha ha this is funny!" You know, walking around and joking around with your friends and shit and it ends up on the record and you're laughing about it. Because when I got sober it was like – I've said this before – but it just was like "Oh shit! I can think straight again!" So I don't know if that record was particularly my best work as far as songs, writing songs that felt like something, that brought some kind of emotion. I ran accents into the ground. I got stuck on that kind of serial killer, crazy vibe and just kind of went with it.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Eminem also addressed the mindstate he had while working on 2009's <i>Relapse</i> saying: "It was interesting, man. I don't know if before <i>Relapse</i>, if we're talking the Infinite album and pre-signing with Dre and all that, from that point on, I don't know if I ever did anything or did much sober at all. <i>Relapse</i> was the first album and first recordings that I did when the lights went on and I was sober. I was still trying to figure things out...It's interesting. Fun time. I had a fun time." and reiterated his feeling about the album "I felt <i>Relapse</i> was, I don't know. I don't know if people know what I really had to go through to be able to make <i>Relapse</i> and to be able to write again and to be able to think again and just normal everyday bodily functions and functions in my mind. I don't want to say I wasn't in a place to record again, but I needed time. I needed time to be able to figure out things. I wanted to be able to make my songs feel like something again. I know a lot of stuff on <i>Relapse</i> was comical and funny punchline jokes, but a lot of the songs didn't really feel like anything. I had to go back and listen to some of my older music to try to figure out what I was doing wrong. Once I felt like I figured that out, I started making songs that felt like something again."<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Complex Magazine included many songs of <i>Relapse</i> on their <i>The 100 Best Eminem Song</i> retrospective, included fan favorite songs like "Stay Wide Awake" on 86 position, "Elevator" at #81, "My Darling" at #79, "Underground" at #74, "3 a.m." at #67, "Insane" at #27, and "Déjà Vu" at #20.<sup id="cite_ref-complextop100_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complextop100-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<li>"Same Song &amp; Dance" contains an interpolation of "<a href="/wiki/One_(Metallica_song)" title="One (Metallica song)">One</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></li>

<li>"Beautiful" contains excerpts from "Reaching Out" by <a href="/wiki/Rock_Therapy" title="Rock Therapy">Rock Therapy</a></li>
<li>"Crack a Bottle" contains interpolations from "Mais dans ma lumière" by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Brant" title="Mike Brant">Mike Brant</a></li>
